## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly explicit time t, which is the standard state-space form of (non)linear harmonic oscillator models. Common physics structures include restoring forces from a potential (functions of x), damping forces (functions of v and/or x), and external/parametric forcing (functions of t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear mass-spring-damper (SHO with viscous damping): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (small oscillations, linear stiffness and linear damping)
- Undamped conservative oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x (energy-conserving linear oscillator; simplest restoring-force-only model)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity with viscous damping)
- Higher-order polynomial stiffness: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) - c3 * v (strongly nonlinear restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping (quadratic/cubic drag): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v * Abs(v) - c3 * v**3 (aerodynamic-like drag or empirical high-speed dissipation)
- State-dependent damping (Li├®nard-type): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - (c2 + c3 * x**2) * v (damping increases with amplitude; common in nonlinear oscillator normal forms)
- Van der PolŌĆōtype self-oscillator (negative damping at small amplitude): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (limit-cycle generation via nonlinear damping)
- Pendulum-like restoring force: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (bounded restoring force; large-angle oscillations)
- Forced oscillator (additive periodic drive): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (externally driven vibration)
- Parametrically excited oscillator (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (Mathieu-type parametric resonance structure)
- Combined forcing + Duffing nonlinearity: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (nonlinear resonance and jump phenomena)
- Smooth dry-friction approximation: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * tanh(c3 * v) (Coulomb-like friction regularized for differentiability)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring force from a potential implies dv_dt depends primarily on x and is often an odd function of x (e.g., -x, -x - x**3) for symmetric wells.
- Purely conservative oscillators (no damping/forcing) suggest dv_dt = f(x) with little/no explicit dependence on v or t, and f(x) typically derives from -dU/dx.
- Viscous losses produce terms proportional to v (dv_dt includes -c * v); stronger high-speed losses often show up as v*Abs(v) or v**3 contributions.
- Amplitude-dependent frequency is commonly captured by cubic (or higher odd-power) stiffness terms in x (Duffing-type), indicating hardening/softening behavior.
- Limit-cycle behavior is often modeled by state-dependent damping multiplying v (e.g., (1 - c * x**2) * v), representing negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude.
- Bounded restoring forces (e.g., pendulum) favor sinusoidal dependence on x (sin(c*x)) rather than unbounded polynomials, reflecting geometric constraints.
- External periodic actuation typically appears as additive sin(c*t)/cos(c*t) terms in dv_dt, independent of x and v to first approximation.
- Parametric excitation is indicated when x is multiplied by a periodic function of t (e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c*t))*x), implying time-varying stiffness rather than additive forcing.
- Dry friction introduces near-discontinuous dependence on v (sign-like); in symbolic regression this often appears as tanh(c*v) or v/(Abs(v)+c) surrogates.

Combine the two linear-in-\(x\) pieces:
\[
= -1.8997465\,v\;-\;3.4380939\,x^3\;-\;3.4380939\cdot 0.0191974\,x|v|^{1/3}\;-\;6.8761878\,x
\]
So GT is exactly a sum of four monomials:
- linear in \(v\): \(A\,v\)
- cubic in \(x\): \(B\,x^3\)
- linear in \(x\): \(C\,x\)
- mixed term with an **absolute value**: \(D\,x\,|v|^{1/3}\)

Crucial structural requirement: any matching candidate must be able to produce \(x|v|^{1/3}\) (with Abs), plus independent \(v\), \(x\), \(x^3\) terms, and **no extra dependence on \(t\)**, logs, sines, rational-in-\(v\), etc.
